Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's**New Maps added 20th Oct 2016**

REVISED 13/1/13

THis link should take you to the album where I have all the current maps now stored. I've been through and updated as best I can. 

Due to the number of maps its easier to do one link rather than keep posting up losts of individual images.

http://s306.photobucket.com/albums/...Falcon_IDs/Latest Millennium Falcon Partmaps/

REVISED 20TH OCT 2016

I've just updated MF002 with the confirmation on the CB750 part from Stu.

Also for ease, here is a link to a new folder rather than individual image links.

https://1drv.ms/f/s!AgdFL5urFwoihV0up7Zb2QFtbWYj

Any problems let me know.

Cheers

Nick

MF009 - 5: Has to be a large scale Kubelwagen. The same piece (only much smaller) is on the Y Wing neck.

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

MF005-Those bracket parts your wondering about are tank barrel clamps. One of the tank kits you've listed will have what you need. All barrel clamps have a top and bottom. All of those you outlined look like bottoms. Hope this helps.

Post #20  (forum post #1498200)
Author    : Flintlock
Date      : Jan 1, 2011 at 1:12 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

Julien, I may be able to help... There's the 8-Rad chassis, a part from the 1:48 Kubelwagen, a few minor bits from the Nichimo 1:35 Jagdtiger, a piece from the Airfix 1:24 Hawker Hurricane landing gear, and a piece chopped off from one of the Saturn V engines. There are also some other Y Wing assemblies on here. One of them is a 1:9 Kettenkrad engine block half with tank treads from the Nichimo Jagdtiger glued on.

[edit] there is also a piece from the Airfix 1:24 Mustang on the Y Neck assembly.

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

Hey thanks guys for all your comments, what a storming kick off. I'll try to update these images soon with the info you've given. 

Hey Lee. Thanks for checking. The '73 Tamiya catalogue has a parts layout for the Matra but I can't see any obvious matches. However the parts are quite hard to make out so you could be onto something. Looks like the pipework I've queried in MF004 look to be from a 1/12 car but can't find a match so far, though the Matra has quite similar parts.

Cheers Whisley on the extra use of the Centurion hull. That's handy then
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Thanks Alan56 on the steer for those brackets, just couldn't get a bead on those at all.

Also thanks for the info that its a 1/24 M60 grill that's used... :cry Had an awful feeling that might be the case. Do you have any other sprue scans you could share for the big M60 so I can try to ID any other parts?

Julien: You are a force to be reckoned with on this stuff (no pun intended) Thanks for the steer on the ship part. I'll start to see what I can find and check back with you.

Flintlock: again many thanks for your help. I consider you to be a real expert at this stuff.

I must be mad doing this with most of my kits in storage, however you can't fight the urge to make big spaceship replicas when it strikes you, especially the MF!

re MF009 can anyone nail that last yellow disk on the side of the docking section. I could call that partmap done then :confused

re MF0010 underside pic, is the detailed yellow engine type part I've question marked, the same as used on the top of the Cylon raider? could it be a 1/12 car like the Porsche 935 maybe?

Thanks again guys. Hope this is helpful to some of you as well as me. Lots more to go yet...gulp....

Nick

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

MF009 Disk - most likely a large scale Kubelwagen (maybe Bandai 1:24). The same part is in the 1:48 (used on the Y Wing neck) and also in the 1:35 Tamiya. Only this one is bigger.

I can't give you a positive ID though, and the scale might even be bigger... But it looks like the same part.

Stu, I'm not sure which KT you're talking about but if it's the one on studioscale.com, keep it mind this one was never used in any Star Wars stuff because it was not available at this time. There is a vintage KT made by Tamiya, it's very rare and Ive never seen any scan of it beside the boxart so I'm not sure if that's the right kit. But seing the copula being molded with the top of the turret, that's probably one of those early crappy Tamiya models !

Hey Julien,

The KT I have is #57 (35057) in the Tamiya MM range, dated 1975, so was around in time for ANH. The turret just doesn't match the part in Nicks parts map.

I don't have any scans of any other 1/35th/24th KT's so really hard to do a comparison lol!.

Kt donor parts are all over the Falcon, but as to which kit from which manufacturer is used is a problem. I'll just have to buy a few KT's & have a look to be sure.

Gort said:

			Hi Folks,

Please see the first of the big 68" Falcon partmaps I've been tinkering up. I've got these all saved as PSD files so I can go in and add/amend to them as required. Plan is that once we get as much as we can ID'd the finalised and 'signed off' maps can maybe go on the Studioscale site for general access and to save people having to keep re-inventing the wheel as far as kit part ID'ing goes. I'm also drawing up a spreadsheet to log what kits are used as a handy reference. Seems like there are also a few kind souls who would be up for casting the odd part from the very rare & expensive kits, which would be a massive help. I'll do the same once I get my stuff out of storage.

There's a hell of alot more to do but hopefully these maps are a start. If any of the kit bashing grandmasters out there like Julien, Lee, Jamie et al can throw us a few bones it would be much appreciated. If you see I have mis-identified anything, likewise let me know. 

As I've said elswhere if/when I get to the point of actually making the big MF I'd be prepared to offer some casts of key areas as a starter kit, however I don't want get ahead of myself just yet!

Seems like there a few folks out there trying to pull this big project off, if we can work together maybe we can actually get it done while we are still young enough to enjoy it! 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

PS: Very sad to hear of the untimely passing of Grant McCune. What a tremendous artist, and what a huge legacy he helped leave to us.

Nick

Post #61  (forum post #1513143)

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

Hi there,

Welcome aboard. I think you may have got the wrong end of the stick on this one I'm afraid. The images I posted are of the original filming model, not anything I have made myself ( I wish). That's the drive behind this thread, to identify what kit parts were used by the ILM modelmakers in order to help define accurate dimensions etc.

The original model hull was made from acrylic domes mounted onto a wooden core. Quite an unusual approach from the typical vertical bulkhead profiles usually done. If you lurk around here for a while I'm sure you will glean some useful information to help you and your father out.

Cheers

Nick

Post #104  (forum post #1580240)

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

Hey, guys!  It’s been a while since I’ve visited the boards.  I spotted your thread, so I thought I’d throw in my 2 cents.

Part #1 in the above pic is from the AMT 1/25 American LaFrance Ladder Fire Truck.  You’ll need 2 kits if using original parts.  It was re-issued a few years back and probably won’t be too hard to track down.

IIRC, part #2 is from the AMT 1/25 Kenworth K-123 Cabover, which fortunately, has just been re-issued by Round 2.  You can get it online for about $30, which is MUCH better than the $100+ it was going for.  And, yes, they did apparently use a second frame part to extend the length, because if ya wanna use kit parts, you’re going to need 4 kits (!).  One of the re-issues came into my local hobby shop, and I think it’s callin’ my name!  I’ll root through it over the weekend and let you know.

Dan
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

O.K. One correction to my previous post - I picked up the Kenworth K-123 over the weekend, and it looks as if I got my rails crossed!  
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
  The K-123 rails match the ones above & below and perpendicular to the LaFrance fire truck rails (#1) and are NOT the rails labeled #2.

Fortunately, I stumbled across my Kenworth Conventional W-925 (Movin' On version) and they match up to #2 (I should've remembered that!  :confused).  The extended bit stuck to the front, however, is still a mystery to me.  I have a few other AMT trucks floating around in my collection, so I'll dig around and see if I can find a match.

Dan

Hi leukirix !

You are right.
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
 We can use Tamiya 1/6 Honda 750CB four.

And Police type.

[edit] However, there are the same two parts because this racer's front disk brakes are on right and left both sides. 

The market type and the police type are each one.

Which moto do you choose ? :love

But we can't use Tamiya 1/6 Honda 750CB-F.(Not CB four) :confused

That part(our needs) is front brake caliper part. This is single piston caliper.

But 750CB-F has twin pistons caliper.

[edit] (750CB-F was put on the market in 1979.)

So, We should take care about this. :lol

(The pic of parts from 750CB four)

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

Hello,

This is my first post here, and it is a question. I hope it is pertinent to the thread.

I have been studying the 5' MF with the goal of replicating it and have noticed that what appear to be bas-reliefs have been cast and repeated on the MF, and some of them used on the Y-wings (as pointed out by others). The attached picture illustrates what I am trying to describe. The green arrows indicate the location of the parts pictured in the larger photos (credits go to the people who snapped them) and the red arrows indicate the repeating nature of the parts in those pictures. Note for instance that the 8Rad/Ketten combo is present on both the "ceiling" and the "floor" of the "cargo bay (what do you call it?)" between the mandibles, and the King Tiger turret detail with all the additional decorations nearby is repeated and so is the Matilda-derived panel.

Upon close inspection, these sections appear to be part of a larger bas-relief from which specific ones were cut-out.

My question (finally!) is: does anyone know where else these are used and what the primary purpose was (e.g. tiles for the Death Star)?
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Post #148  (forum post #1607490)
Author    : Gort
Date      : Mar 24, 2011 at 6:15 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

Tell me about it. I'm sure a couple of guys around here know, but it seems to be one of those Holy Grail type mysteries. I think its a kit part due to the two little bumps on the top leading side.

Its such a curious and fiddly little part to have made. Generally they tended to just apply the kit parts from the box with maybe a bit of cutting, but when you look at the original Kettengrad part and then how it ended up its quite a tricky little bit of work. I guess they really wanted it to match the concept design feature and made the extra effort. Lord knows what the second donor part is. Maybe we'll come across it one day....
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

Hi Dr Tak,

I put it down as an Italeri Kubelwagen simply as it looked a good match.

[IMAGE: Kubel_bonnet_s.jpg]

I've seen alot of Kubels with the bonnet wheel mount having a hole in the centre as opposed to the little 'nipple' as shown on the ILM model. This tooling looked pretty good. It also matches the same appearance of the Bandai Kubel bonnet which is placed just next to it.

However, you are way better informed than me on all this stuff so I'm happy to be corrected.

Cheers

N

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

Just a note regarding the Bonanza kit.  It was originally released by Entex.  The molds were also used by Bandai.  At present, they are released under the Minicraft label.  Same goes for the Piper Cub (which is used on the Galactica) and the Cherokee.

In other words, these kits are (thankfully) readily available - and relatively cheap.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

SSR said:

			Just a note regarding the Bonanza kit.  It was originally released by Entex.  The molds were also used by Bandai.
		

Click to expand...

Hi guys,

Though I apologizes to upset the talk, that was originally released by Bandai.

Entex's 1/8 Porsche RSR was originally released by Eidai Grip.(See the kit sprue. There must be a stamp of "Eidai" in it.)

J.P.S. Lotus and Mazda rotary engine were too. [Edit: Mazda rotary engine was reliesed by Gakken. Unsure.]

It seems to have sold Entex by repackaging kit of various manufacturers.

And more, Itareli's Steyr tractor was originally released by Max-mokei.

MF020A

The manufacturers are "Aurora","Airfix","Esci","Revell","Monogram","AMT/Ertl","Otaki","Arii","Mitsuwa","Eidai-Grip","Nitto"...

"Aurora" had it. But this one is not correspond.

"Otaki" had it too. Not correspond.(Arii using the mold of Otaki's)

Info: There were 3 type kit of Tamiya's King Tiger.(Not include present issue.)

They seemed to have changed the mold on the way.:cry

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

Keep the good work, folks. I am in admiration of such dedication and passion.

The Nichimo 1/35 Jagdtiger appears to contain the part marked with a question mark in MF019.

Regarding the 1/6 Honda CB750, it is the Racing version that is required. The parts of interest are mirror images of one another, and they are used in their entirety, partly obscured by the 8 Rad assembly. In some shots of the deck, you can even see the tiny "pins" protruding on the sides. There are a couple of other parts nearby on the sprue, one of which being used on the port side, around the base of the mandible. See attachment.

On another topic, from 1970 to 1979, Tamiya did have a very small line of 1/48 models called Mini Tank Series. However, the series did not include the King Tiger. So that deck is still a  :confused

Are we sure it is 1/48 scale? Back in those days, there were 1/50 scale kits too...:rolleyes

Post #305  (forum post #1675736)
Author    : Dr TaK
Date      : May 12, 2011 at 1:52 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

BlackPig said:

			I don't know the Tamiya's Mini Tank Series. Do you have these kits ?

Could you please show us the box.
		

Click to expand...

I don't own any of the kits in this series. The information I have is from various catalogs.

I am aware this is rather a digression since it does not help us with the deck we are looking for, but I can provide the following details.

Initially, between 1970 and 1972, the series included 8 models: T36/76, SU-85, Swedish "S" Tank, M60, M60A1, M60A1E1, Kanone and Japanese MBT 71.

Some of these were re-issued in 1979, and Japanese Type 74 was added in 1980.

A couple among these were re-issued in 1994 as part of a new line called Remote-Controlled Mini Tank Series.

While I have not seen any of them in person, I believe the more recent Advancing Mini Tank Series is another re-incarnation of some of these tanks, but this time as completed models.

The only German tank in all these series is the Kanone. A picture of the box circa 1971 can be found here, and the 1994 re-issue here.

In fact, Tamiya did have a couple of armors at 1/50: the T-92 Airborene Tank and the Crusader II, released in 1967 as part of a line called Pocket Museum Series.

Again, sorry this is not really helping much other than to eliminate Tamiya from the radar.

Post #309  (forum post #1684073)
Author    : Dr TaK
Date      : May 18, 2011 at 4:02 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

Dr TaK said:

			I don't have a Handley Page, but do have the Tank Transporter, so I'll check on the size relative to that kit part.
		

Click to expand...

Sorry for the blackout, have been recovering from a hard disk crash.:angry

Based on the KT/JT kits at different scales in my possession and furious amounts of calculations, the verdict, at least for the time being, is that the part under consideration is neither 1/48 (as measured on Bandai kits) nor 1/35 (as measured on Tamiya kits), but somewhere between 1/38 and 1/43, perhaps 1/40. I learned that Fujimi used to have a line including a KT in this scale. Other manufacturers also released armors at 1/40, but I have not been able to identify any JT/KT as of yet.

It could also be the case that the part is from a model whose size was not very accurate, and add the fact that back in the day, sometimes a manufacturer would decide to label a kit 1/48 or 1/35 depending on how popular a scale is, regardless of the actual size of the model.:rolleyes

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

MF 020A

Mitsuwa 1/48 Hunting Tiger appears to be closest in terms of features. I still need to get my hands on a Handley Page for size comparison, although I may be able to check against a Pontoon Bridge.

Also, I am not entirely sure how the hull was cut, as the part seen on the MF appears to have a margin where the turret starts.

The kit has been re-issued in recent years by Aoshima with a slightly modified tooling for the hull bottom to accommodate their gearbox. The included remote box is also different but could be the same as the one that Mitsuwa was offering separately.

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

Hi everyone!

Gort I found the tank deck for MF022:love! It comes from the Tamiya 1/35 Chieftan MK V. It's a section cut out of the hull. A part of the same section is seen in the middle of the butt of one of the Y-Wing models. 

 I am not sure how the section used is cutted off from the hull, I need more pictures.

 In MF010, partrs #1 are from the Centurion except for the one resting beneath the Revell 1/32 Phantom landing gear, It belongs to the Chieftain too. They can be found inside the Centurion bottom hull too, behind the Sherman part.

 And just above the Chieftan parts there is another part from the Bandai 1-48 ZgKw 8Ton.

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

Hi Gort, hi to everyone!

  Here is the first section of the 5 foot Falcon blueprints I am drawing.  My Idea is to make a complete Blueprint of the falcon, with every kit  part drawn to full detail.

   I started with the inner mandible because I have most of the kits used  in this area and the big Chevy 57 donor part is very useful to  estimate measures. 

  I estimated the height of the mandibles -without counting the Kenworth C  123 parts- to be in between 5,1 and 5,2 cm. If anyone has a different  calculation please let me know.

  The Idea is to complete this blueprint with the help of all of you.  Comparing notes and sharing pictures of the kits needed. The  mandible section counts with one part drawn thanks to the help of Black  Pig who kindly post the picture I asked him with measures of the part of the Honda CB750 used  on the right mandible...Thanks again BP!:thumbsup

  As you can notice there is a part missing on my blueprint, the American  LaFrance Chassis part. If any one can help me with a good scan of that  part and the measure of its length and height it would be great.:love

If any of you guys posting in this thread wants a full resolution (200dpi)

real size version of this section of the blueprints send a mail and I will send it to you!

hikaru84@gmail.com

  I will continue to post the blueprints as I advance, and with the help  of Gort and his work, and all the Falcon-addicts posting in this thread I  am sure we will nail this fine spacecraft!

[IMAGE: innermandibleblueprints.jpg]

Uploaded with ImageShack.us

[IMAGE: innermandibleblueprints.jpg]

Uploaded with ImageShack.us

 I scaned the top view picture of the Falcon from my Chronicles book (OUCH!) but the offset printing blurs the details so we need a better source.

Post #345  (forum post #1755858)

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

The 'earliest' pics I'm aware of in a publication, of any quality, of the Falcon in it's 'original' condition, were in the 'Famous SpaceShips of Fact & Fantasy' magazine dated 1979 published by 'Scale Models' magazine as a one-off special for the UK market, but then was released in the US by 'Kalmbach' publishing. 

The pics were just mouthwatering back then & still hold up today & do show what the Falcon looked like 'New' .

I think for my build, it will be in ANH configuration with the 3 landing gears, not the 5 as per 'Empire'.

Pics of the underside in her original 3 gear config are just darn hard to find!.:cry

Stu
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

This was made on the original ANH model ... they never build another 5ft falcon.

  Maybe it was one of the asteroids?:lol

Hi Chris, hi everyone.

Heres what i've found looking at some pics.

It seems to be the same radar dish and base. The thing is that the base is turned 180° now a days from when Star Wars was filmed. So the detail we see on the screen caps of the support on the dish are now looking to the cockpit side of the Falcon, and the dish is been turned upside down as one can see looking to the wethering spots I circled in red in the picture below:

[IMAGE: mfradardish.jpg]

Uploaded with ImageShack.us

 In the pics taken now a days you can also see the little spots were the railling used to be pasted on the Saturn V part. All these leds me to believe it is the same radar, what do you think?

The pic with the yellow frame is the Big Radar Dish Model.

 What remains a mystery to me is what did they use for the Radar Dish :confused

Anyone knows?

Click to expand...

 

For the most part they used handles inserted into the side walls to carry, lift and maneuvre the 5ft'er. It has 4 attachment points (holes, as seen in the attached image below) on either side of both docking rings where they inserted the handles which can be seen being used in the above image.

That doesn't mean they didn't put their hands directly on the model but it would have limited the number of times they need to do this. These holes were not covered during filming either.

You are right.
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
 We can use Tamiya 1/6 Honda 750CB four.

And Police type.

[edit] However, there are the same two parts because this racer's front disk brakes are on right and left both sides. 

The market type and the police type are each one.

Which moto do you choose ? :love

But we can't use Tamiya 1/6 Honda 750CB-F.(Not CB four) :confused

That part(our needs) is front brake caliper part. This is single piston caliper.

But 750CB-F has twin pistons caliper.

[edit] (750CB-F was put on the market in 1979.)

So, We should take care about this. :lol

(The pic of parts from 750CB four)

I'm glad I was able to id one for you guys 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
 I have so many of the kits needed for the Falcon. Funny thing is, if you're building anything from Battlestar Galactica, you have what they had to build Star Wars! I'm currently in the molding phase of my studio scale Base Star: Studio Scale Base Star - Resin Illuminati

I haven't updated the thread for a while but the project is in the molding process. The first parts for the prototype are coming this weekend. All the floors and then the walls and then the larger panels. I'm actually getting excited about it getting so near the kit phase. But thanks to the Base Star and related Galactica models, I have many of the common and rare kits needed for the Falcon! I am looking to build the ANH version but will also build the added structures to be able to add and remove, via magnets under the skins and in the landing gear boxes. I will only be missing the weathering around the boxes but,,,,,, but I can add and remove them, as I want too 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
 sort of a 2 for 1 build ;-) I have to say you guys are a super group and I hope I can contribute more ID's. 

Thanks for allowing me to be part of your group!

Thanks Nick. I spent the weekend going through all my 1/72, 1/76 and 1/48 kits looking for parts on the guns. I found two little parts from a 1/72-1/76 US half track. Strange thing is, there is the back of a half track aft of the gun in front of the grill detail that looks like a Stug vent. I looked thrugh all my 1/35 Tamiya half tracks, both long and short box releases, no luck. It appears to be more inline with a 1/48 scale at largest based on the two small parts I found. I have already checked my Bandai 1/48 half track, not a match. I will shoot picts of the small parts tomorrow. The guns and it's surrounding structure and area are hard to find good picts of without the damage to them. 

And I still have to shoot picts of the Heller 1/8th Honda CB750FOUR. It's a vintage kit with a kit number of L983 on the box.

Post #381  (forum post #1848967)

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

I posted the Heller CB750FOUR because of the earlier conversation of the CB750FOUR being used and what kit was used. I posted these so the guys that were looking for the CD750FOUR info had another option to look through. The one bike was a later release, post Star Wars I believe, so this was a kit that was out and I was told a couple were in the shop so, I scanned it and hope it helps 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Now, the Galactica used a couple motorcycles also. One is a large scale Motorcrosser tha Mike Salzo has and used on the shuttle as it was used on and the gas tanks were used on the Galactica. I have to dig out the other bike kit but it was also a off road cycle. I bring these up because the ILM, Apogee, Universal Hartland and MCA 59 guys had these kits around from past project and added to the collection as they did more shows/movies so my thinking is, some of the kits could be reverse sourced so to speak. In some cases, I know a real good molder and caster to do the cost restrictive kit parts. I was thinking of doing the 1/24 Bandai parts and the McLaren M23 parts. Not all the McLaren parts, only the ones specific to its particular kit. The rest of the engine parts are the same on several of the Indy Cars that used the Ford F1 engines. He's doing my Base Star castings and all I can say is, fantastic castings. I received my first set this weekend and all I can say is, top quality as he does vac is rtv and pressure his castings to 85psi till cured so, the result is very clean. I will ask him to drop into the thread and then the parts can be made and sold through him as I'm not doing them, I’m only lending the part that are needed to him to make available to you all. I hope this helps because this birds expensive to build!!!

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

[IMAGE: MF005_nose_frontcopy.jpg]

[/QUOTE]

The Yellow parts that are bordering the top center structure is part of a cut down frame. The lower structure has a frame that borders it and is from the same kit. The parts on top are what was cut off from the frame. It's from the Frauhauf fuel tanker. If anyone has this kit, pull the frames out and look at them. I already cut mine down. You will see a real long set of frames. On the end of them is a section that steps off to the side of the frame. If you look at it, you will see all the markers that confirm this part is a trimming from the part that is used on the bottom center structure. If you cut the part off right where it meets, you will see it is exactly like the parts pictured above.  The other parts is from the Bandai 1/24 Panther. 

Sorry to have been so long winded. I'm just trying to make an image without a picture of the parts.

Mark

I forgot, the part numbered 12 appears to be from a 1930 era vehicle most likely from Monogram. I have the Rolls Royce from Monogram and it's not the correct kit and neither are any of the Johan 1930's cars. If you look at the one Apogee shop picture, someone drew an arrow pointing to a kit and made the remark they wished they could make out the kits. I believe that is the kit the inline 6 motor part came from. The Rolls Royce kits engine is close.

Not sure if this was yet posted. In case not, yet more Sealab:

[IMAGE: large-scale-millennium-falcon-kit-ids-dsc_8233-copy.jpg-69214d1317096822]

These are two of the main frames of Sealab, back to back. The arms that go around the habitat are trimmed off (those are used as the angle braces on the corners of the docking rings, but that part is well known). 

This is starboard side only - the upper piece has a flange on the right for equipment to attach to. The port side uses two of the lower type. (Edit: no, there is one of each type on both sides of the ship. No idea why I thought that.)

Edit, here's the piece itself:

[IMAGE: large-scale-millennium-falcon-kit-ids-01010701.jpg-69216d1317097363]

Hi guys!

 I've been out of the loop for quite a while, but never stopped doing research on the 5 footer.

 I have a question for all of ya! Anyone knows the exact length of the Falcon?

In the Star Wars to Indiana Jones book and in other publications it is said to be173 cm in length, which is 5 foot plus 8,2 inches.

 I've made some calculations and it seems to be quite a precise measurement when compared to the classical top view picture of the Chronicles book, but when compared with other pics it gives me less length.

 Anyone has made calculations on this subject?

Rod

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

Hi Rodmart, I'm curious, too.  I got the same calculations - just based on the only part I have - the Wankel rotary engine, which is visible from the top view.  It's a crude method I guess - just measured how many Wankels long the ship is - and got the same 163cm length.  Try measuring the cockpit diameter against the Wankel - I got about 6 inches, which is what some members here said it should be, based on available materials of the day.

I hope someone can share any other top view shots - the classic one is distorted in some spots like areas of the mandibles.  I don't understand how it would be possible to distort the photo this way, unless the 5-footer was built like this -  with wonky maintenance hole alignment.

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

For what its worth, way back when, I got much the same as crackerjazz, using the same method. The Wankel engine. I didnt have the actual engine like crackerjazz has, but the specs on the net at the time were spot on. A three way balance in Auditing is considered a garantee of a balanced, so, if we can get another measurment from another part as jedimaster has suggested with the (m23 parts and the 312b) then one could safely assume it is correct.

I know I dont offer much assistance (cant afford the kits) but I check for this thread every day, and the job you guys are doing just blows me away. 

I may never get the chance to build a 5 footer, but the detail I am able to get from your work will help me scratch every part for a AMT/MPC size build.

Now thats enough wind up ya $#^$^, get back to work.

Thanks again

Ozzy

Post #448  (forum post #1981119)
Author    : Nwerke
Date      : Nov 4, 2011 at 1:59 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

Hey Crackerjazz, I was working on my drawings last night and struggling with that distortion issue. It's not the only distortion either, seems as if the port upper docking tube surface is longer than the starboard upper docking tube surface, for example. This ship was thrown together as a late rethink build, so maybe it is just wonky.

I'm distrustful of all the measurements from the Japanese books (BotLA and Chronicles). Some are just totally off and some seem like they may have been done in ways surveyors and modelmakers wouldn't consider (running a tape along a diagonal or kinked edge, for example). 

Right now I'm STILL getting 64" (162.5cm) overall, based off the engine vents being 4" and the maintenance pits 3". But that still gives me 6" for the cockpit tube! Still waiting on a Wankel in the post, hope it gets here soon...

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

Ozzy it sounds like you are talking about parallax. The main problems are that we don't know the lens used, nor the distance from the camera. There's clearly a fair amount of parallax in the photo, so it wasn't taken with an ideal lens or at an ideal distance for our purposes. I doubt it was literally taken looking down on the model - more likely with the model mounted vertically. The camera was *reasonably* perpendicular to the model's datum, but (I think) not perfectly.

Also, the camera's angle relative to the datum wouldn't account for the *skews* in this picture.

Simon, I now make it 47.5" diameter for the sidewalls. The acrylic shells obviously a bit wider than that. Don't have a dim yet.

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

Cheers, Rodmart. I've done a bit of rechecking and fiddling on the turret height and hull centre depth now. Hull/turret total height is 0.9583 of turret diameter (or very very close - I have good grounds to say this).

Would you say the turrets are 12" diameter or close? I get 12.014" at my 67.5" overall length or 12.13" at 173cm overall. 

If that is about right then the turrets are 0.75" high on a 10" deep hulll, for 11.5" total depth. 

Of course the turrets are closer to the camera than the edge of the hull, so they're slightly exagerrated. Ngggh, that thought's doing my head in, I need to go to bed. Have fun guys.

Nice Job Nwerke!

Thanks for the tips

 I've got similar diameters for the gun turrets mate. I scaled the Sculpting a Galaxy turret pic using as a guide the Centurion part now missing.

It gave what you can see in the pic:

[IMAGE: gunportdimentions.jpg]

I calculated for the plexy a diameter of:12,78 cm / 5 Inches

 The cockpit tube gave me a similar diameter 15,24 cm /6 inches

 Now I am trying to calculate the measure of the hull height and as Simon  mentioned above the differences between both upper and lower hulls.

 If the acrylic sheets were worked just by heating them and blowing them  up to get the dome shape it is almost certain they are not symmetrical.

  I think this asymmetry is what gives the Falcon that aged and realistic look.

 bests

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

Scott, several builders have tackled the problems. One guy even did it pretty much before the Internet. The problem is that those guys basically achieved the feat by buying *every single kit that was in existence in 1976*, and checking for donors. So I guess some of them may tend to feel that us Johnny-come-latelys can bloody well do the same thing. 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Lee, the hull *armature* is made from a laminated timber ring. The plexi shells are heat-formed, supposedly blown. Could be a couple of other processes too but whatever they did, some refs seem to show that difference! Could be more distortion but hard to account for it any other way.

Keeping in mind that nothing is square and no panel on the port side is the same size and shape as its opposite number on the starboard side! Much lulz to be had.
		

Click to expand...

 

For the plating I went with .060. The thickness appeared to be the same as the sealab parts from a crossection view near the loading ramp. I mic'ed out the sealab parts as close to .060 +/-. I also used .010 for the pods plating.

I never used the topside view of the falcon in such books like the chronicles. The turret is inaccuratley viewed towards the overall length. But we already knew that. 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

By the way...

Which falcon are you guys working on?

ANH or ESB? I was contemplating ANH, cause in my opinion, that was the untampered "original." No flood lights or landing gears. No flight sticks("how do you fly it?" -Harrison Ford interview)

But then, wanted lights for display at night. I wanted to display it landed and the gearbays somehow made her seem "tougher" :love  Added a "top hatch".  Made a second comms base for the damaged for the death star II tunnel run.

Reactions : Like — Bjorn
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

The 'spokes' are different too, not by much, but just enough difference to notice.

I'm struggling at the mo with the small differences in the Ford F1 engine parts, trying to decide just which kit they came from. Just when you think youv'e got the right part & re-check with other ref, turns out, no, not the correct kit. 

I really want this prop to be as faithful as possible to the original, even going so far as to have as much 'original plastic' as possible &  less resin casts. Expensive yeah, but this will probably be the only one I would do that for.

For example there's at least 4 vintage Tamiya 1/35th Panzer 111 Ausf M/N's on her, 2 on the engine deck alone as best I can tell so far.

I can really see why this prop has taken a fair while for the guys who have steadily been working on her to do, most of it I guess is acquiring the donors over time.

Hats off to these 5' pioneers for sure.

Stu

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

Hey rod!

Great job!

However, you should break it down to:

Base

Armor plating over base(dome) - Mandibles sector diameter

Dome diameter(overhang from base) hint:sealab part and sidewall donors indicates added width - see pic below

And finally overall armor plating diameter past the dome overhang, rather than just main disc

Just makes building easier.

Post #544  (forum post #1998481)

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

Hi again Brotherhood of the Falcon:lol

I forgot to post these pics. I thought the Falcon blueprint from the Star Wars Blueprints Book was for the Full Size Falcon for the Hoth Echo Base. But a closer look revealed that there were kit parts from the "ANH" Falcon in the drawing.

 So I compared the Chronicles picture with the blueprints and got the Blueprints book data you find on the chart above.

Here are the pics:

[IMAGE: falconbpch.jpg]

Uploaded with ImageShack.us

And between the interior and exterior blueprints:

[IMAGE: falconbpbp.jpg]

Uploaded with ImageShack.us

The main differences I found were 3.

1-The joint between the disc and the mandibles. Even though this blueprint might be correct because the lower dome finishes earlier that the upper dome in the mandible section of the ship, but I still need to compare it with the bottom view "forbidden to post" picture.

2-The gun turret disc is smaller

3-The section of the Aurora M8 carrier is wider

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

Rod- Thanks for posting those blueprint pics mate. I really feel they are not of too much use to us SS builders though, as they really are drawings of full sized set pieces. Best we do our own group blueprint.

Can I suggest this to all the 5' Falcon builders here. The info & ideas brought to this thread is staggering & I feel we have a great group who may like this idea?.

Why not each one of us take on a section of the Falcon & focus on that area specifically. Meaning, take me for example, I do the engine deck, place & collect all the donors I can & then draw a definitive blueprint for all to share. Means we focus on 1 area & then each others areas can be brought together as a whole.

Now, with this idea comes the loaning of kit donors from members of the group to each that need specific parts to complete their area. When the blueprints done the parts are returned to their owners.

Take my engine deck. I need the M60A1 parts, kubelwagon & M8 Dozer Blade just to 'finish' the deck off to an acceptable level to be able to draw a decent blueprint.

Some of you may have collected donors for a specific area & virtually have a section done, that would be great, just needs to be 'dry assembled' & drawn. 

Does this sound a feasible idea guys?. It may speed things up too for us all.

Cheers

Stu

Current figures:

Main Disc (w/plating): 50"

Inner Walls: 47.53"

Feathers 1: 52.079"

Feathers 2: 47.535"

Mandible Sector: 48.5"

Turret Roof:  12"

Turret Base:  12.25"

Turret Window: not tackled yet

Docking ring - as above

Radar Dish: 6.5"

Maint Pits: 3.125"

Cockpit 1: 6.25"

Cockpit 2: 3.79"

Cockpit plexy: ?

Hull height: 10"

Turret depth: 0.75"

Hull + Turrets: 11.5"

Mandible: 2"

Side walls: 2.5"-3"?

Upper Dome: 3.75" (including plating)

Lower Dome: 4.17" (including plating)

Front ('wide') edge of jaw: 5.95"

Height of front panel of jaw: 0.78"

Rear panel of jaw: 7.68"

Top panel of starboard docking tube: 14.83" x 3.98"

Top panel of port docking tube: 14.89" x 3.98"

Can't swear to any of these...need more kits!

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

It's the same as the sides. Just the crescent shaped front to which the mandibles attach that is slightly higher. You don't notice it with the plating overhang. So the mandibles and sides are two inches all round. But the wall the mandibles attach to is slightly higher to accommodate the overhang... If that makes any sense at all???

Post #559  (forum post #2003138)
Author    : Nwerke
Date      : Nov 16, 2011 at 2:47 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

It's not JUST the plating overhang - as in RM's picture above, the acrylic shells themselves are cut back at the mandibles. 

The shells also overhang the wall at the waistband, but not at the mandibles - only the plating overhangs the wall there.

Simon, more than 2.2" I think - this applies underneath too don't forget.

EDIT: also, the thickness of the domes themselves forms part of the wall at the mandibles section.

Sorry, no idea. The original K-rad pieces are cast, by the way, did you notice? Don't cut the K-rad bits down too far btw - the mandible versions only have the sump removed while the maintenance pit ones are more heavily trimmed.

Oh the mystery chassis rail on the outer port mandible is made up of three separate pieces. The very front is a separate part. It's a replacement dating back to before ESB.

Another correction: EIGHT!

The detail in the port rear maint pit is a cut-down copy of the inner jaw detail - with the 8-rad chassis and hull sides...and each of those has another two Kettenkraftrad engine halves.

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

Simon, not offhand but have a rummage in F1 bits I'd say. 

BTW don't bother with the Flak38 or Panther bits for the inside detail plate for the jaws - they're only on the lower one, which has been cut up as part of the modifications for adding the landing lights, so not correct for Star Wars. 

Nick, some of the M23 tie rods are re-used a lot, including at spots on a couple of maps you've already done - see pics following. Be careful because you only get four of these in one M23 kit and you need four of them separated and cleaned up, *and* another four still attached to their own sprues for the docking tunnel, so don't cut them free for that application...
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

Not that! Anything but that!!!!! Well, almost anything. Big boy.

Unfortunately these pics are embargoed, I believe. I've been mulling over whether or not to respect that given that the person selling them is also selling a bunch of my photos, amongst other pics by various usual suspects, on the same disc. Leaning towards '**** that for a game of soldiers', but I'll probably take another couple of months to make up my mind.

Then again, having seen 'em I can say they're not THAT desirable anyway. Monochrome, not a long lens, rather 'casual' placement of the rule and they have some DOF issues - a very narrow field depth, so a heck of a lot is OOF. IMO they're definitely more useful to Star Wars modellers than anyone else.

Hi Chaps,

The small purple parts are from the Nichimo Jagdtiger. See Studioscale for sprue picks. These actually sit on the sprue right next to the blue barrell support noted in the pic. 

I think the green part is from the ESCI 1/9 BMW 75 motorbike which is already used alot across the engine deck.

Hope that helps. I will catch up properly with you guys on this at some point next year when I can get a chance!  :confused

Nick

Regarding measures for the gun turret, these are the measures I keep getting, I can't see how it could be any bigger chaps?.

Turret roof: 280mm / 11.02"

Turret base: 290mm / 11.4"

Height: 19mm + 1.5mm plating = 20.5mm total

Window Diameter = 112mm / 4.4"

Now, the detailing strips which surround the turret sides, I thought were originally from a 1/35th Sdkfz 251/1 Rocket Launcher. Of course this is too big. 1/72nd seems to fit perfectly & I found Esci did one, probably a vintage kit too. Found this photo of one, what do you guys think?.

I agree. The La France bits sit on the side not the top so it makes sense. Having said that nothing on this bird is even. A part that sits at one mm on one side , sits at 3 mm on the other. Another interesting fact is in the b&w ANH pic you can clearly see the gap between the end of the chevy chassis and the start of the pontoon. The gap looks at least 5 mm which would mean my original mandible length is out. Also as Martyn said. The 8 rad chassis doesn't appear to be a complete one. I think it's chopped. A la y wing. The other part is used elsewhere.

Post #672  (forum post #2016664)

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

It is definitely chopped mate. I'll try to find the pic that shows the edge lying under the Chevy.

BTW the La France pieces sit on BOTH the side AND the top. They have that deep rectangular plate which goes over the top, while the rest of the rail is on the side. Well...IN SOME CASES. For example the lower starboard rail is mostly on the side, but the upper starboard one is mostly sitting right along the top edge of the mandible - corner to corner, in cross-section terms.

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

Updated kit list/map index. I've separated maps into separate columns, which bloats the document but is easier to read even so (I think). I've included all of Gort's maps, most of Rodmart's and various others, with preference given in that order where there are overlaps.

Some kits that have been discussed remain unmapped and I have listed them as such, or as "speculative", whatever the balance of evidence suggests. I'm sure there are errors; this is a work in progress as much as the parts mapping effort itself, so, please feel free to offer corrections or suggestions.

Simon this should help a bit with the Hummel parts hopefully.

The big Tamiya CB750 Racing. There are three variants - police, civilian and a cafe racer. Guess which one is rare, expensive...and the only correct one? :unsure

Edit: there's the CB750F as well, which is a later kit that's completely different. The Police and Civilian versions do have some parts which were used but only the Racing has all of them. It's currently most commonly available as a pre-built.

To my knowledge no one has identified what angular piece has been added to the kettengrad part. Post #791  (forum post #2043168)
Author    : Nwerke
Date      : Dec 12, 2011 at 1:21 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

Rod, nice find, we're killing those maintenance pits lately! 

Ozzy, yes and no. They USED to be identical (and it is the same casting in the port rear upper maintenance pit), then the model was rebuilt for ESB. The FlaK and Panther parts were added to the lower jaw then. 

Alnitak, that is the beauty of her! She's the queen of the coated-in-glue-and-rolled-in-kit-parts ships. 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
 (Aside from all the other SW ships equally worthy of that title, of course.) 

Quick warning for us 5-footer newbies: be really careful when taking kit parts off the trees. MANY of them retain small tags of sprue and some of them even seem to use them as spacers or details in their own right. Don't trim them closely when cutting them from the sprue as you would if building a kit! 

There are even some parts with additional moulding points (those little circular tags that don't attach to a larger sprue) still in place. I'll post an example of what I mean later...
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

Cheers Craig, good going there! Oh sod, hard to get hold of that kit, what with all the dern TIE Bomber builder fighting all the dern Probot builders for it. :lol OTOH I might still have most of an old one somewhere in my parts stash. I used to break kits up into 'like' bits, which was a stupid approach in retrospect but back then I never expected to be building any replicas.

Oh - it's the Ladder Chief you really need, btw. Well, Fire Chief will also supply almost all the really visible bits. 

As for finding bits, honestly it is like a smorgasbord right now...it's not that I have any special talent at this, I'm just buying a lot of kits! It would be difficult NOT to find a lot of parts. :lol And there are doubtless a ton I have missed so far. When we get down to the small stuff that's when I'll really falter, you just watch!

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

As we turned to Iding parts we left aside the dims we were looking into some pages behind.

 There were differences between the dims of the gun turret. Since I got the M36 Jackson I found out that there is this part pasted on the side of the turret, part that measures 1,9 cm / 0,747 approx in height. This gave me a turret depth of 4,27cm / 1,681" plus 2mm of styrene sheet! Way off from the 1,91cm /0,753 or 1,73cm / 0,68" we were guesstimating before!:wacko

What do you think of this Martyn, Stu, Craig, everyone? :confused :confused

[IMAGE: turretheight01.jpg]

[IMAGE: turretheight02.jpg]
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

Hi Rodmart, then the part's length would be 5.5cm?  The turret top width looks more than 10 times that part - which would turn out to be more than 55cm (21 inches) wide if that were the case.

Maybe there is a similar smaller scale M36?

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #865  (forum post #2059014)
Author    : Nwerke
Date      : Dec 21, 2011 at 8:10 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

1.9cm x 35 = 66.5 cm high in real life. Divide by 72 gives .92cm high. Divide that by 1.9 = 0.48 x 4.27cm = 2.06cm or .81". I think the part is from a 1/72 or 1/76 kit. Is that one more for the list, or a scale correction for the existing one?

There's a more direct check. One of the rectangular M23 plates that is used all over the engine deck is on the front of the lower turret, mounted vertically. Try scaling from that as a crosscheck.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Post #896  (forum post #2071569)
Author    : Nwerke
Date      : Jan 1, 2012 at 7:28 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

Nick, cool, can't wait. I go to your maps first and then pore thru everyone else's but it is getting a bit hard to keep track of. E.g. I thought I was first to find those winch halves on the halftrack turret part that's next to the Elefant grille, but was pathetically late to the party there. 

For the StuG, you want the original 70's kit. Item no. 35014, a.k.a. 1/35 Military Miniature Series No. 14, per attached pic.

Avoid item no. 35197 which is a new tool IIRC, ditto anything with "Fruhe version" or "Early Production" or "Late Production" etc - those distinctions were not made by plastic kit firms until what, the early 90s or so.

The Schurzen ("skirts") are in 35014, I can't say for the others, my armour lore fails me there. If present they are likely to be from new masters.

Post #905  (forum post #2075718)
Author    : Nwerke
Date      : Jan 3, 2012 at 11:32 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

There's a dimensional issue with the top view pic showing the naked turret (what IS that thing, anyway? Can't be the blank for the turret itself, surely; those would have been detailed and painted at the same time as the hull, no?) 

Anyway, keep in mind that the turret is located on a plane that is four or five inches closer to the camera than the plane defined by the edges of the hull. And the edges of the hull are a good 20 inches outboard of the edge of the turret, so as the crow flies the distance is greater again. Thus the turret appears larger than it is in relation to the overall hull.

There's another missing part too, by the way; a small square grill directly below the replacement for the missing left Semovente part. Is it original, or part of the fixups? All part of the mounting point cover and must have been beaten up repeatedly. 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Oh, also, the Valentine part sits on a square of styrene that actually projects forward off the edge of the turret. Beware that! As for pics, the "SAG" photo does show the full fore/aft length of the turret, with the full length of the Valentine part also visible.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Post #912  (forum post #2082728)

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

Martyn, Here's my turret measures mate, I'm going with these & my gun barrels set will based on these measures. I'm confident they are ok, especially since the hanomag parts are ID & fit ok too.

Turret height: 22.5mm

Turret base:   11.5" (292.1mm)

Turret top:     11" (279.4mm)

These turret measures are virtually identical to yours mate, so I think it's a done deal?.:cool

I feel the top plate is 2mm styrene & the actual plating would be 1.5mm styrene.

What I'm doing at the mo is, Im drawing up the whole top plan view of the Falcon in 1/1 on a piece of board & tweaking it with all the kit parts & measures I have on hand. This will act as my blueprint & all other views will come of this. I will share this quite happliy to all, but please don't ask me for a copy, bit hard to put through the scanner.:lol

This is good for the engine deck especially, as it's sooo complicated to line everything up on a piece of thin card or paper & move around as needed.

Stu

Post #913  (forum post #2082784)
Author    : Nwerke
Date      : Jan 8, 2012 at 6:37 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Large scale Millennium Falcon Kit ID's

Thanks Stu, good to know! Rod's dias were a bit smaller and for a while mine were too, but after trying my darndest to account for the distortion, I still get so close to 11" front to rear that I think it HAS to be what they were using. I think the plating thicknesses you gave are the best match we could obtain in our parts of the world - even if the originals were odd very-slightly-larger Imperial sizes that we can't get, it won't really show anyway!

Re plan views I couldn't agree more, I'm more or less doing the same albeit in 3D. Specifically, I have a 25"-radius styrene semicircle on which I'm building an engine deck contour mockup in urethane foam, so that I can space the parts as accurately as possible. Easy to modify and once tweaked can potentially serve as a forming buck.

Another small part find, Tamiya 1/35th Panther Ausf A.

Just a thought regarding the Tamiya 1/12th F1 kits used on the Falcon.

The M23 is THE major donor of all the F1 kits used, how about if the parts maps label the part as M23, as first choice,  over all other F1's, unless a specific part is indeed from a different version & is deemed unique. I know the DFV versions are spread over a number of kits, but the M23 is generic.

An example would be parts map MF 012 1.2, part #4 is labeled Lotus JPS, but these parts are found in the M23 as well.

Stu

Staring at Sealab parts some more... my initial hunch about the radar dish was correct and those are actually the #36 railings! I didn't have those parts in hand initially, only the incorrect #35 part. Fixed that problem and now have a Sealab with most parts still attached to the sprues. :cool

The rods on the docking ring that I thought were just cut styrene are actually part #s 50 and 85.

Since the ILM guys used a bit of plumbing (PVC) etc, It occured to me they most likely just used a stink pipe cover for the cockpit canopy. I tried to find one that fit my AMT many years ago but all too big. When discusing this topic with another falcon builder I sought the advice from an old plumber friend of mine, and when showed a pic of the cockpit, he was prety much convinced it was just that. He even had a specific name for the type (Stubby nosed type). Apparently they still make the same (simular) type in the USA.

Ozzy

I couldn't help myself sorry, got 2 more of the M23 G-sprue, from that ebay seller. This sprue hadn't been available for quite some time, so I grabbed a couple. Only needed a few parts from these, but I'd rather have the original plastic as much as possible.

Panther arrived yesterday, 4 days from Japan, a postage record I reckon:lol. Usually when a kit arrives, I delve into it with the sprue cutters, cutting off all the relevant parts & placing into clear plastic bags, corresponding to their position on the Falcon. I might just leave this kit intact for a while, it's just so blooming fantastic. It's a mint one too, all parts still sealed in bags, even the 3 tubes of glue. I still think Bandai made some of the best kits ever & still hold up today!.

Hi guys
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Here is a correction for the MF003 Map. The part circled in red does not belong to a ford engine F1 1/12 but to the good old Centurion, you need to cut it as shown in the picture.

[IMAGE: centurionpart.jpg]

I'd just like to comment on kit 7 above: there was no tamiya sherman in 1/35 scale that had these parts back in those days. They made an m4a3e8 that had different suspension parts. These are probably from the M36 or M10.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #998  (forum post #2135684)
Author    : Rodmart85
Date      : Feb 14, 2012 at 11:29 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

That's right Scott. Those suspension parts can be found on both Tamiya kits, M10 and M36 Jackson. 

 The suspension of the 1/35 Tamiya Sherman is similar to the Hasegawa 1/72 Sherman used in the X-Wing and in the Docking rings of the 5 footer. What I am not sure about is if the Sherman Suspesion used on top of the Centurion chassis behind the rear landing gear of the 5 footer is the Tamiya 1/35 M4A3E8 Sherman N°18 or a bigger scale tank :confused

Post #1014  (forum post #2140779)
Author    : -... . .- --..
Date      : Feb 17, 2012 at 8:48 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

No sweat at all, Martyn. This is actually just a part of the collection I use to identify parts for both ANH and ESB miniature projects. Luckily for anyone building the ANH Falcon, you won't need to worry about the Hasegawa rail guns or the Entex Porsche (very, very lucky on that count :cool).

Well, at least not until things on the five-footer started getting modified for ESB, anyway, in which case it makes sense to be looking at some of these later kits as well. Same goes for the original Star Destroyer, which picked up a whole bunch of new parts for ESB. Depends on what versions folks are planning on building.

There are a large number of donor kits that have been mentioned in this thread that you'll see in this shot. There are other kits that are in that shot that haven't been mentioned yet, but probably will sooner or later.

As much as anything, I wanted to give folks a look at a portion of what they're going to need on hand to actually build a five-foot Falcon the old fashioned way. A bit of inspiration mixed with a dash of reality.

Post #1024  (forum post #2142243)
Author    : Nwerke
Date      : Feb 19, 2012 at 9:55 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Beatlepaul, if you're asking which tank kits can be used to scale down from the full size? The answer is 'none', I think. The big Falcon is about 1/24 and uses mostly 1/48, 1/35, 1/24 and 1/15 armour kits. 

The MPC is about 1/96 or four times scaled down, so you would need to find equivalent kits in the 1/192, 1/140, 1/96 and 1/60 ranges.

Incidentally this makes the Fine Molds about 1/144. 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Sure are. They're cut, though - the five-panel schurzen are cut into sections of two and three panels. A number of the Panther parts are modded, which is why I am moulding them - I figure not everyone will be too keen to cut and mod originals. These are on MF010 1.1, btw.

Post #1058  (forum post #2154693)
Author    : raiders
Date      : Feb 28, 2012 at 10:43 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

eagle1 said:

			Great work on the rings Craig, bet you can't wait to get the 3D parts to assemble.

I have a small leaflet that Tamiya thoughtfully put into their 1/35th military range after reaching the 150 models mark. That was 1991 when they reached this point. It's very useful as it has all the serial #s & pictures of the completed models in order. I'm still not clear though, as to why the Duster & Sheridan are not listed, obviously donors for the Falcon during the original build?.

Guy's, amazing ID's going on here, just incredible.

Stu
		

Click to expand...

 The Complete Works of Tamiya Volume 1 states that there are two different series for 1/35 scale. 

  One series was called the “Military Miniatures series 1/35” and kit no. 76 (British SAS Land Rover “Pink Panther) to kit no. 92 (British L.R.D.G Chevrolet) were released in 1976 and kit no. 93 (SU-122 Russian Assault gun) to kit no. 101 (German Flak Panzer IV Mobelwagen) were released in 1977.  The first armor released in this series was in 1970 (British Army 6pounder Anti-tank Gun, kit no. 5).

The second 1/35 series was called the “tank and armored car series”.  The M42 Duster (kit no. 27 released in 1970) and M551 Sheridan (kit no. 31 released in 1973) were part of this series. Kit number 46 (British Army Chieftain Mk5) was the last kit released in 1976 (August) in this series. The Russian KV-II Gigant kit no. 47 was the only kit released in 1977 (February). The first kit in this series was released in 1961 (German Tank Panther).

I’d be happy to give further information on any other Tamiya kits in this book. Keep up the excellent work.

Post #1065  (forum post #2157471)
Author    : raiders
Date      : Mar 1, 2012 at 9:29 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Tsophika said:

			Raiders, what does your book have about 1/25 kits from that timeframe?

Craig
		

Click to expand...

 The Tamiya 1/25 series started as 1/21 scale, and there are only 14 kits in this series.

  No. 01, 1/21 US Army M4A1 Sherman 1963

  No. 02, 1/21 US Army Self-propelled artillery M40 Big Mutt 1963

  No. 03, 1/21 US Army Heavy Field Piece M2 Gun “Long Tom” 1963

  No. 04, 1/21 German 75mm Assault Gun III Sd. Kfz. 142/1. Sturmgeshutz III, Ausf. G. 1964

  No. 05, 1/21 PzkW3 German Medium tank Sd. Kfz. 141 Panzerkampfwagen III 1964

  No. 06, 1/25 German Army 45.5ton “Panther” Sd. Kfz. 171 Panzerkampfwagen V 1966

  No. 07, 1/25 German Army 46ton Medium Tank Jagdpanther 1967

  No. 08, 1/25 British Chieftain Battle Tank 1967

  No. 09, 1/25 Russian T34/85 Medium Tank 1969

  No. 10, 1/25 Russian Tank Destroyer SU-100 1969

  No. 11, 1/25 German Panzerkampfwagen VI “Tiger I” Sd. Kfz. 181 Ausf. E. 1969

  No. 12, 1/25 Panzerkampfwagen V “Panther” sd. Kfz. 171 Ausf. A 1972

  No. 13, 1/25 Jagdpanzer V “Jagdpanther” sd. Kfz. 173 1972

  No. 14, 1/25 British Army Centurion MK III 1972

The books are in Japanese, but there are lot of pictures of box covers.

Now, been looking hard & long at the Semovente gun parts on the top turret. I'm now certain they are not from the Tamiya kit!. Some of the detail on these parts just doesn't match up to the ref I have.

Hi Craig, I do not know were the notion that the Hasegawa Morser Karl kit was not used in Star Wars ( ANH ) came from, But I found some time ago a circular shaft on the rear landing gear that belongs to this kit. 

 Being this part found on one of the black and white pics it might be said that this Hasegawa kits were on the ILM stash on the late 70's, here is the pic:

[IMAGE: morserkarl.jpg]

The sprue pic is on the wrong side but I am certain it is that kit part.

 I have noticed that the color session of pics like the ones used on the AMT Falcon kit box or the ones on the Chronicles book seem to had been taken before the B&W because in the later there are kit parts missing that can be seen on the color pics. 

 It might well be that that wheel belongs to the Morser Karl or Leopold kit. I must take a look

Post #1120  (forum post #2269447)
Author    : eagle1
Date      : May 22, 2012 at 5:32 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Hey Rod, I'd also wondered about that part from the Karl too, but never checked to see if it's right. Well, I just dug it out & placed it on the Panther part & also checked my ref & I'm positive it's from this kit. It is a match IMO.

I don't know either with the notion this kit wasn't around in the ANH era. I can't confirm for certain either way. The only thing I can think of was the B/W photos were taken quite a while after ANH, but before 'Empire'. The Karl part could have been added during this period & not being an 'original part. This would explain a few of the other missing parts that show up in these 'early' B/W photo's, such as one possibly from the 312b on the starboard side mandible wall.

IMO, the Falcon got pretty beat up in storage between ANH & Empire so new parts were added & somewhere during this period the B/W were taken.

Stu

Stu
		

Click to expand...

My minicraft catalog from 1977 lists #728 Anzio Annie rail gun and #732 Thor (Morser) 60 cm rail mortar as being available .

The squadron mail order catalogue from spring 1976 (no. 10) lists only 728 Anzio Annie as being new from Haegawa. No mention is made of Thor.

From the above I would speculate that the Haseqawa Thor (Morser) was released sometime between summer 1976 to December 1977. Minicraft Models INC. was based out of Torreance, California and was importing some or all kits directly from Hasegawa.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

I was going to put this in Eagle1's 5ft Falcon build thread but did not want to detract from his epic adventure.

Anyway, I was looking at some new images of the cockpit of the 5ft Falcon when I realised something interesting that I had never noticed before. I just thought I would post this in case others like me, weren't aware of it.

The cockpit has a cap at the front of it and where I had previously known of the "scalloping" of the edges I didn't notice the hexagonal shape around the centre window. It's only just barely discernable in the first image so I highlighted in the second image below.

[IMAGE: mf_13a.jpg]

[IMAGE: mf_13b.jpg]

However, it can be seen more clearly in this image.

[IMAGE: Cockpit3.jpg]

I thought I'd share how I started to set up the radar dish as it's kind of a tricky area. This is how I interpret it, so I'm open to thoughts if someone sees it differently, haha! Here I have two parts from the 1/15 StuG and a cone from the Saturn V. Notice you can see a lip from the edge of the StuG piece, which wouldn't be present if it was trimmed any other way, I think. Glued together and sanded flush to the rocket cone.

[IMAGE: attachment.php]

It's a lot of work for an area that you don't even notice. Going further down to the base, you'll need a bunch of parts from the Hummel, StuG, Harrier and Handley Page.

[IMAGE: attachment.php]

Hi there guys, long time no see!

 I was watching again the SAG DVD last week and realized that the top pic of the 5 Footer that appears in the DVD is not the same one as the one in the Chronicles book :eek :eek.

 I do not know if everyone here knew, but is cool to know that we may still came across some new reference of the Falcon! 

 It would be very nice to have this pic in hi reso, but this is the best I could do, here is the cap:

[IMAGE: falconsagdvd01.jpg]

As you can see this pic has less shadow and you can clearly see the edge of the cockpit and the gun port is there.

Post #1195  (forum post #2793166)
Author    : maruska
Date      : Mar 10, 2013 at 3:36 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

I've just started clicking through this thread, and without sounding like I'm shamelessly plugging my own thread (which is here, fwiw) - I'm working on a project to fully digitize all the parts required to make the Falcon - especially the rarer ones.

Once in CAD form, any of the parts can be printed or machined at any scale. Want a 5' falcon at 32" scale? Easy.

Full scale? Crazy - but plausible.

I'm currently creating the full scale interior set pieces (at full scale - but with the intent of fabricating them in miniature) and will be eventually moving on to exterior bits.

I'm looking for collaborators, or people that have access to kit parts. Just thought I'd share.

... And thanks for all the great part identification here - it helps a lot!
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #1196  (forum post #2793997)
Author    : eagle1
Date      : Mar 11, 2013 at 4:47 AM

Hi maruska, thought I'd chime in here mate.

I'm well aware of your incredible cg work on the Falcon, namely the cockpit interior.

Now while I admire your work very much & where it ultimately ends up, 3D-printed parts, I'm choosing not to go down that road for my build. Everything that isn't a kit part will be scratchbuilt, the, how shall I say it, old school way. That's just me, I'd rather have the satisfaction of handcrafting parts.

But, if you need help with the donor parts for scanning etc... I'm glad to help. 

Stu

Post #1197  (forum post #2794008)
Author    : ozzyguanche
Date      : Mar 11, 2013 at 5:04 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Hi maruska,

Although I do not speak for anyone else but myself, I thought I may respond as someones who has "not" collected the many kits involved in building a 5 foot falcon.

I understand that the work you see here is a number of years work for some people as well as many thousands of dollars to those who have purchased the kits to identify the parts. Some say well over $10,000 US to secure the majority of the kits needed. The 32 inch Falcon no less involved.

That is a significant investment for anyone in time and money for any project let alone a model. To hand over that knowledge and hardware so someone (anyone) can just print a copy would be I think, a difficult thing to ask those who have invested so much. 

Love your work, and admire the fact you are putting it out there for everyone, as I have done myself, but although there is much sharing within the falcon building community, I dont think a full list of parts will be physicaly made available so as anyone can simply print a part at will unless you purchase every part yourself.

Hope it is taken the right way, could be wrong!

Regards

Ozzy

Post #1198  (forum post #2794313)
Author    : maruska
Date      : Mar 11, 2013 at 9:20 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

eagle1 said:

			Hi maruska, thought I'd chime in here mate.

I'm well aware of your incredible cg work on the Falcon, namely the cockpit interior.

Now while I admire your work very much & where it ultimately ends up, 3D-printed parts, I'm choosing not to go down that road for my build. Everything that isn't a kit part will be scratchbuilt, the, how shall I say it, old school way. That's just me, I'd rather have the satisfaction of handcrafting parts.

But, if you need help with the donor parts for scanning etc... I'm glad to help. 

Stu
		

Click to expand...

Thanks, Eagle!

This project for me is really just a different form of kit bashing and scratch building. I already have hundreds of hours invested in research and CAD-time as well as piles of model kits in hand - and I still have to build the darn thing. I expect this to be several years just in the digitizing, let alone the build.

I don't plan on making a fully assembled digital falcon ready-to-print. It would be cost prohibitive and the part clean-up would a total nightmare - so it's still parts - no different than using castings - just from a digital source.

I also see this as a bit of a preservation effort. After losing several eBay bids on high-ticket model kits, I thought myself: I have 20 years design and CAD experience I should just start building this stuff. At the part level, much of it is easy - it's the aggregate that becomes the model.

Anyway, I'll PM you to see if there is something we can work out.

[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

I am glad to see you opening a window, maruska! 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
 There is a place of honor for the "old-schoolers", and they deserve the highest level of respect for their dedication and efforts. But there IS a modeling revolution beginning, similar to the beginning of the electronic age... I think it is just as important to explore these new methods as it is to preserve the old ways.  So never allow yourself to be dissuaded by those who are un-willing to addapt and colaborate.  And you don't need anyone to give you anything... all the kit ID's there are, to date, are on the net somwhere.  You may just need to join a few more forums to access them.  Good luck with your project.

Post #1204  (forum post #2795225)
Author    : eagle1
Date      : Mar 11, 2013 at 6:14 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Hmmm, I'm at a certain age, ahem, that will still have the ' I'll do it the old ILM way, with an armature built from the more traditional materials & original kit parts added for detailing'. That's fine at the moment & the foreseeable future, but eventually the donor kits, especially the rarer ones, will run out & start to not even appear available, even after years of waiting/looking. Heck, even now some kits just do not come up, they have probably become 'extinct' to put a word on it!. 

On the flip side to what maruska is offering, which I'm all for & I guess he's trying to get across is, to have an inventory of printed parts that will be around forever, to give folks the chance, say in 50 years away, to build a 32" or 5' Falcon for themselves. 

I myself prefer the actual kit part to use as opposed to even a cast, but even today it is just not viable to do so on a limited budget. I have a ton of duplicate kits just so I can use the'actual plastic'.

But, even ILM, cast/injection molded parts too, as they had a budget as well. 

Sorry for derailing this thread Nick, need to put more actual ID's in here real soon mate!.

Stu

wow,

What an interesting Thread...still getting caught up ...

But I just wanted to say:

Thanks! to all those who have done such a great job identifying kit parts.

I am utter amazed at all the hard work and Keen eye, and diligence for  such a task.

I had  been milling over in my head for the last 3 years and I've decide to go ahead and try my Hand at a 5 footer too. :wacko

Already had half the kits ...Been gathering up the harder to find kits for the past 9 months

 I'm glad to see others taking the 3D/CAD Cam approach to supplement traditional techniques 

-that is one area that I hope I can contribute too  --perhaps with some 3D parts but also some 2D Cad work for laser cutting etc.

[IMAGE: 78981-18f9a1cf080d2ad3a968b4a3e0fe7721.jpg]

[IMAGE: 78980-48a9b9ea5675070103541b3d89f0cc96.jpg]

[IMAGE: 78979-2eac5372af3a7fc43fce2309a6e8b0bb.jpg]

[IMAGE: 78943-92cd63e953226b6357d8295a5cd01b48.jpg]

[IMAGE: 78982-73ddd20d8fb4c9c09b09d4ad7058b9a7.jpg]

[IMAGE: 78971-8d3e6ced0c45809493a8897479f14ac9.jpg]

[IMAGE: 78968-eb6325c4aa28702a7fbf2e6d7bab7d20.jpg]

[IMAGE: 78983-a709894903a990d59914da3a70fe05f3.jpg]

Here's a small  sample of parts made from other projects

On the greeble/ kit parts front -I've been building up quite a Library

I respect Stu for wanting to Scratch build everything but for me sometimes the best use of my time is to use Laser-Cutting, Stereo-lithography,CNC Milling and other Rapid-Prototyping techniques.

Of course it's a balancing act: with the budget too , while 3D print can be cool..it is not always the cheapest way to go

For my own Build I'd like to have the Cockpit & Gun-Turret bays emulate the full-size sets (ANH)

With the plethora of very talented traditional Scratch-builders on this board;  I hope I can lend a hand to the MF builders community  with some 3D/CGI/CAD  tools brought to bear on this subject

Heya Mike,

Awesome you're going to enter the frey & do a Falcon mate, I hope you know what you're in for:lol

Just to clarify my build a bit: I'm using original kit parts as much as possible, buying multiples of ones that are feasible to do so.

Some are not feasible & I will be casting copies. My goal was to always have as much actual plastic as possible & I'm still sticking with that.

The hull & substructures yeah will be & are built from scratch of course from acrylic & styrene with a metal armature.

There will be no printed parts at all, no CNC milled anything!. Old school I guess
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Your build will be exciting to see evolve Mike, being a completely different approach by the sounds.

Either way, we all end up with a 5' Falcon in front of us, yeeha!.

Stu
