Post #1234  (forum post #3222926)
Author    : eagle1
Date      : Feb 27, 2014 at 4:43 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

You can count on any help you need Mike with your Falcon build when you are ready.

I'm going the vac-formed hull panel route as well, makes sense as you only need to make a section as a buck & use for the rest.

I have decided that I will no longer offer parts that I make as 'parts sets', as there has been little to no interest in what has been offered in the past by me. That's not a grudge, but rather a realisation that the 5' Falcon is a very 'limited' wanted model by the model building community. I have done the engine vents/gun turrets & offered as parts sets, really it fell on deaf ears, there just aren't serious enough Falcon builders out there. Therefore I will be making the future parts for my build & offering to the 'group' of 5' Falcon builders if they want them, no problem.

The Falcon I guess, is such a 'boutique' model that interest is high, but actual builds will be low, similar to a Galactica.

This is what makes the Falcon 'special', well, to me it is, the 'grail' of all ANH miniatures. 

Stu

Vacformedhero said:

View attachment 494069I am trying to do a detailed build of the pit areas , as I'm building the ANH version I have a question over a missing part , it should have sat over the hatch on the jagdpanther section, I have only ever seen this in the chronicles book , out of focus , and on a resin kit someone supplied here, is anyone aware of the part?

- - - Updated - - -

Here is the image from page 47 of From Star Wars to Indiana jones
		

Click to expand...

Hey, that looks all the world like a 'tow ring' component from a tank kit.  On German WWII tanks, anyway, a pair would often be incorporated in the vertical hull plates or attached to them, with the small 'holed' part projecting forward for a hook to grab into and then to the tow cable loop... so probably a tank kit.

Hope this is a small help...

R/ Robert

----------------------------------- Updated:

Sorry, I thought the part included the object below it and to the side, but upon closer look I see it is just the trapezoidal shape with the hole. Puma turret floor perhaps?  Nope, too small really.  Model ship platform? Gun mantlet component?

Thanks Robert , I've been scanning a lot of sprue images for kits identified as have being used and others that were not, initially I thought it might be the machine gun mount on armoured vehicles but the shape seems wrong, then when viewing sprues the centre assembly for field guns look close if one leg was cut off, but I think this kit may be from an F1 kit that supplies a lot of parts, my birthday is coming up and I hope to acquire this kit so I may be able to confirm if the part I saw on the sprue shots is the right one, I'll let everyone know what I find .

the other item from these maps I think needs correcting is the m23 piece glued across the port side of the front mandible , I believe this to be the piece in front of the upper turret just in front of the guns and when the gun was damaged someone stuck it on the port side as it looks similar to a part on the starboard side. The missing part on top of the Jagdpanther hull in the upper, rear starboard pit is I believe Ferrari 312b, so yes, its F1 related.

If like me you're building an original ANH Falcon with all the missing bits added, then you'll need 2 of the M23 part. Gun turret one is as is...I think...from memory & the mandible sidewall part was cut down.

Post #1269  (forum post #3834196)
Author    : asalaw
Date      : Dec 4, 2015 at 9:52 AM
Reactions : Like — blackeagles
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

blackeagles said:

			Hi friends,

I hope you are well and that your editing progress.

I have two quick questions , because I block a bit to my beginnings :/

What is the differences between :

8'0 '' and 8 ''? in metric system.

second question, concerning the radar dish .

I have a "plan" (a picture I had posted here by the way) on it, 

the base of the radar base is 4'00 '' ... 

but I 'm not sure of that by the different post on the forum, because there is not indicated in diameter ... 

Do you have an idea ?

View attachment 562346View attachment 562347

Click to expand...

8'0" is 8 feet, 0 inches. 8" is 8 inches. 8'0" = 2,438.4 mm; 8" = 203.2 mm. I believe the diagram is full size measurements, not scale measurements. In full size, 8 feet looks about right for the dish. 1 inch = 25.4 mm.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Checked around and yes, Revell GMBH has the Matchbox molds.  That is how they were able to reissue the old Matchbox 1/48 SH-2F Seasprite kit.  Also why a bunch of the (as marketed by REV) "new" armor kits are to 1/76 scale... just not with the multi-color plastic sprues anymore.

R/ Robert

Post #1285  (forum post #3891597)
Author    : eagle1
Date      : Jan 30, 2016 at 12:42 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Yes that is Thompson Ong's Falcon...its a beautiful build & his more recent posts are incredible.

Note though that it is not accurate to the 5 footer in most areas. He has taken the blueprints from either the DK  blueprints set, or the print that came with the deagostini part kit, you can see it on his wall.

So his model is of a 2 X 32" based model. He has used bis own kitbashing everywhere as well.

I love it though & his skills are admirable.

The member here that built the SS Executor also has a 5 footer build. Beautiful build there as well, but again, not an accurate shape or part for part replica.

Stu

Post #1296  (forum post #3891667)
Author    : maruska
Date      : Jan 30, 2016 at 2:00 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

motionminded said:

			For me the 5' blueprint is my bible also, I even got my baseform made... stil have to redo the domes. Did things change a lot?
		

Click to expand...

Not sure yet. It started with reassessing the tube diameter (6" instead of 5.75"). That has a slight ripple effect on the rest of the model. We're still working through it. Fortunately our master model is parametric, so we can look at variations pretty easily. Then we run them through a photo match process to verify the model. Photo matching has a lot of variability, so usually we'll get things to where they are solving pretty consistently before we release the next version.

Guys like Eagle1 have really helped us pin down known dimensions with part layouts. Thanks to everyone who has contributed!
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

eagle1 said:

			Yes that is Thompson Ong's Falcon...its a beautiful build & his more recent posts are incredible.

Note though that it is not accurate to the 5 footer in most areas. He has taken the blueprints from either the DK  blueprints set, or the print that came with the deagostini part kit, you can see it on his wall.

So his model is of a 2 X 32" based model. He has used bis own kitbashing everywhere as well.

I love it though & his skills are admirable.

The member here that built the SS Executor also has a 5 footer build. Beautiful build there as well, but again, not an accurate shape or part for part replica.

Stu

Post #1355  (forum post #4031435)
Author    : Gort
Date      : Jul 16, 2016 at 11:11 AM
Reactions : Like — ProfKSergeev, asalaw, McGraph
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

When I worked at the BBC Visual Effects department in the 90's and we could see the growing impact CG was going to have on traditional effects techniques, especially miniature VFX stuff such as Red Dwarf, I and a colleague of mine Mike Tucker, began to do exactly what Knoll talked about on Friday. i.e making up virtual widgets ( or greeblies if you are Stateside) with which we could detail CG versions of Dr Who or Red Dwarf ships etc. In the end the work began to get grabbed by smaller cheaper outfits so we never got to really develop our traditionally informed approach to CG. 

Nice to see that the top guys at ILM have looked at the work on this forum and elsewhere and arrived at similar conclusions. Mind you, they probably look at the part maps and think we are all nuts for doing it, but hey...

Jaitea said:

			Just to comment about images from this thread that were shown in the John Knoll presentation at Star Wars Celebration yesterday.....he showed the portside mandible with all different coloured parts similar to the image above

He was using the images to illustrate the fact that his team at ILM have made 3d models of many greeblies as CG components for future model making in the virtual world,....all those Tank & F1 kits

J
		

Click to expand...

I think 27heaven was talking about the BF109 engine frame, not the landing gears. Author    : Gort

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Thanks for the part ID notes guys.

As it happens I managed to ID those La France parts the other week along with the cut down 312B part which sits on the front of the same panther box. I got those from looking at picks which I think Stu posted of his build a while ago ( thanks Stu!). This is why I'm trying to update and review the previous maps so that we can all re-group and focus attention around the remaining parts that really are unidentified, (at least in the public domain) and quickly document the ones that are in fact already known.

I'm spending a bit of time trying to ID parts on the top surface for the new MF011 map, but I know that whilst I'm discovering parts that are new to me, I doubt I'm finding anything that hasn't already been ID'd by someone else here; which of course isn't very efficient. However, I'm conscious that its not fair to keep expecting people who are further on with things to keep having to help out, even though they are always very generous with their information.

Once I finally get MF011 as far as I can take it,I'll highlight the parts that are stumping me and then ask for everyone to dive in, critique what I've done and see what we can nail.

It does feel that a huge amount of progress has been made on the Falcon over the years and the number of really elusive parts is definitely shrinking.

Its been a turbulent and emotional few months on the SS forum from what I can see, so its good to know that there are still some keen 5' Falcon ID'ers out there  
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Nick

Post #1452  (forum post #4147156)
Author    : 3Dsf
Date      : Dec 21, 2016 at 5:18 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Hi, folks! Would anyone have any visual leads on a greebly that was present on the 5 footer during the ANH era, but which has subsequently been lost?

 Sorry if this has been covered, but I couldn't find any reference to this topic in a scan of the thread. In fact, I'm not sure what the deal is for identifying kit parts that are no longer present in any modern-day reference photos! Feel free to delete this, admins, if it's been covered.

 The part is on the five footer, at the top of the jawbox near the dorsal gun turret. It's next to the missing trapezoidal vertical piece, pierced with a few holes, that's been identified as part of the suspension of the Tamiya 1/12 M23 McLaren. The trapezoid has been replicated on the TFA digital model, apparently minus the smaller holes.

http://www.therpf.com/attachment.php?attachmentid=674079&d=1476803948

http://www.indycals.net/blog/wp-content/uploads/IMG_3505-300x209.jpg

 But then there's a sort of hand-like or vaguely Y-shaped horizontal piece, that goes into a hole in the trapezoid at one end. This has been at least partly replicated on the TFA Falcon.

 At some point both these bits fell off, since they only seem to be in 1977-era photographs, and current exhibition photos have only blank spots. The 32" model has a three-lobed part where the hand-like piece is found.

[IMAGE: 375799-c76daabdd6bcc69494cb1d13fa7dff21.jpg]
 
[IMAGE: 375800-0820e0bfebfab703a7ab077ee68d82a5.jpg]

 A good visual reference for this missing bit would be awesome. Thank you!

 Thanks!

[IMAGE: https://www.therpf.com/forums/attachments/cannon-part-1-jpg.692033/]

[IMAGE: https://www.therpf.com/forums/attachments/cannon-part-2-jpg.692034/]

Post #1475  (forum post #4456183)
Author    : Lab
Date      : May 5, 2018 at 12:10 AM
Reactions : Like — 3Dsf
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Hello, I am new to this thread.

I am not sure if this is already covered, or if it is appropriate to raise in this thread, but I came across certain details that I noted while studying reference photos to reflect on my Bandai PG Falcon build.

They are to do with parts A & B in the pic below:

[IMAGE: 467249-07e3ba873b6573eb0e51d607ad712cda.jpg]

Having seen this photo with Richard Edlund,

[IMAGE: 467250-548b78734c8a6e054c3ec2818704b5a4.jpg]

.. which was taken presumably when these were shot (he is in the same shirt, and the antenna dish looks as though they are facing the same angle),

[IMAGE: 467251-c8b3c6a9224355fb9436b00439acf7c2.jpg]

[IMAGE: 467252-5d9c1c23e439c60fd9b9e3faff628c66.jpg]

.. I wondered if it is safe to assume that part A was broken and part B did not exist there during the shoot of ANH.

Taking a closer look, there seems to be a smear which suggests that part A was in its original "V" shape when it was first attached, but are there any info or views, as to whether part A was broken by accident or with intention ?

Looking at part B, I had the impression that it looks as though it was misplaced when it fell off from a different part of the engine deck (there are two or three of these parts which seems to have fallen off). Comparing the area on the opposite side it seems that the part was not there when the model was being weathered.

Portside:

[IMAGE: 467253-2fe7e8694463d141ff2f8de4d9bce3d8.jpg]

Starboard:

[IMAGE: 467254-36e7bb3049c21b583b325ea00c6b3bd7.jpg]

I thought there could be several interpretations as to whether part B was initially left out by intention, or simply forgotten, or it was originally there but fell off before the filming.

Are there any info or views on this part as well ?

Post #1477  (forum post #4456496)
Author    : t2sides
Date      : May 5, 2018 at 5:27 PM
Reactions : Like — chazzychaz, Sparky70, Lab
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Lab, Welcome!!   Good sleuthing there.  

So yes, it does appear B was indeed there around the time of filming.  SW Chronicles shows these two B&W pics that seem to be taken during ANH filming, and B is indeed there, in some other same time/era pics, it is definitely gone.  So, as it goes with us builders, you have to make concessions and decisions of what you want to put down. If you want to be ACCURATE, you would be correct having it in place, and not having it in place 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
.    As for A, all the known evidence shows it was always broken. 

For my build, because I agree the little shadow is evidence the whole part was there and got broken right around filming time, I chose to put the entire part on mine, as I like the 'balance' to both sides.  Hope this helps a bit.

(EDIT - Lab, you've caused me to think this through a bit more, and after re-watching the TIEs attacking the Falcon after they leave the Death Star, and consistent with the Edlund Blue Screen photo - I've now decided I will remove the B part on that side, and chop up the strut!!  I love this kind of feedback to get you re-thinking things, thanks!!)

[IMAGE: 467403-81053dd7c79eeff272bcc5eb08b06902.jpg]

[IMAGE: 467401-0977883c0e385e594a479f8f35385792.jpg]

My build with Part A and B on

[IMAGE: 467402-522d023d5892179004bb2dbf402d0b91.jpg]

Sparky - that ring part on the walkway is the Bandai 1/24 M60.

Click to expand...

Thank you very much on your comments.

Your build is spectacular. And your photos make it clear that the colors of the styrene that gets exposed in the chipping process shall match the original, which is only possible by going through the trouble of obtaining the original parts.

As to the B&W photos, it is written in page 55 of the Chronicles book (2017) that they were taken by Dennis Muren on 30th October, 1978.

Another pic that indicates that part A was in its "V" shape when first attached.

[IMAGE: 467432-d279faf3f839b27ee36076b7f6a886c5.jpg]

It is of course probable that the part was accidentally broken at some point.

However, the more I look at the breakage point, as well as how it is left attached, the more I feel that it is more natural to interpret that the part was snipped (upon some intent), not snapped, even if some accident was involved.

[IMAGE: 467433-d43608dfe4ddc33bff8debea306519bd.jpg]

This pic of the other side also makes me feel that part A was 'broken' and part B did not exist when the model was weathered, which is indicative that the modellers must have been conscious about the state of those parts, and at least decided to leave it at that, even if some accident was involved.

[IMAGE: 467434-62b960f7ed92e2e76851f2b53fbdaa88.jpg]

Post #1526  (forum post #5116468)
Author    : Bjorn
Date      : Sep 24, 2020 at 1:30 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

There are others but try these:

[IMAGE: logo-og.png]

						Millennium Falcon parts for 3d Printing
					

Hey all,   I'm a long-time lurker with a long-time Falcon project sitting on the bench. Much of my approach for my Falcon thus has involved machining and 3D printing of parts that I either can't find or can't afford to kit bash from; I do a ton of CAD work in my job, so it's a natural extension...

[IMAGE: favicon.png]

					www.therpf.com
				

[IMAGE: logo-og.png]

						Limited Run - 3D Scans of 150+ Star Wars Confirmed Donors
					

As the hobby gets older, and the original confirmed donor kits get scarcer, and thus more expensive, the ONLY solution to this growing problem, and to this hobby having a future in which future generations can make these incredibly detailed, enjoyable, and massively complex builds, is to...

[IMAGE: favicon.png]

					www.therpf.com
				

Some parts are already published on GrabCAD. The rest are in the works. There are only a few contributors so it's a long slow process.

Cheers,

Post #1533  (forum post #5206857)
Author    : Bjorn
Date      : Jun 18, 2021 at 11:12 PM
Reactions : Like — Sparky70, Studio Kitbash
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Like many others here I have searched long a hard to find the same piece in a donor kit with no luck. 

Recently I have been examining photos of the underside of hull. After looking more closely at these pictures, I think it's just Styrene, or at least the very outer layers with patterned holes, likely by hole punch.

Here is a closeup of the starboard fwd landing gear box (photo courtesy of Nwerke).

[IMAGE: https://www.therpf.com/forums/attachments/screen-shot-2021-06-19-at-3-49-52-pm-png.1468611/]

Some of the same holes are found in the armour plating around the gear cutouts.

I'm not sure if this has been covered but there are also featureless circular styrene pieces similar if not identical in diameter to the punched holes. Likely the recycled punched material placed back down.

I'd bet that Eagle1 has the correct approach to replicating this detail in his build with styrene card.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #1534  (forum post #5206889)
Author    : Studio Kitbash
Date      : Jun 19, 2021 at 6:41 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Very interesting -- I never noticed til now how the larger circular "punch-outs" were then recycled and added as additional layer greeblies on these and adjoining styrene panels - but which totally makes sense with ILM's "use as much as you can, don't waste anything" build philosophy. 

It looks like two standard size hole punches were used -- any clue what those dimensions are?
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
